# 1. DESIGN PHILOSOPHY & CONCEPT

## Core Narrative

**"The Gate"** explores transformation through the lens of Slavic/Eastern European mythology, reimagined through a Southwest American perspective. The journey moves from chaos and trial (Baba Yaga) through a moment of crossing (the transformation ritual) into transcendence and arrival (The Great Gate of Kiev).

**The Three Acts:**

**Act I: The Trial (Baba Yaga)**
- Chaos, uncertainty, the unknown
- The Hut as a symbol of wandering, searching, being tested
- The Assistant's attempted escape and return = acceptance of the trial
- Musical character: rhythmic, percussive, unsettling, dynamic

**Act II: The Crossing (Transformation Ritual - Finals Only)**
- Silence, stillness, choice
- The shedding of the old self (jackets, hats)
- The revelation of what lies beneath
- This moment exists only at Finals—the season shows skip directly from Act I to Act III

**Act III: The Arrival (The Great Gate)**
- Resolution, transcendence, homecoming
- The Gate as threshold, not barrier
- Musical character: triumphant, warm (Finals: mellophones lead), overwhelming
- Season: joyful, human ending
- Finals: sacrificial, profound ending (DM's exit)

---

## Why This Narrative Works for The Academy

### Regional Resonance
The desert Southwest shares mythological DNA with Eastern European folklore:
- Wandering through harsh landscapes (desert = steppe)
- Spirit trials and transformation
- The crossing from the profane to the sacred
- Gates, thresholds, and oases as symbols of arrival

### Underdog Story
The Academy's journey mirrors the show's narrative:
- The Trial = years of building, competing at 15th-18th place
- The Crossing = this show, this moment, this choice
- The Arrival = breaking into Top 6, then Top 3

### Member Investment
The transformation isn't just visual—it's psychological:
- Members experience the ritual themselves (removing jackets, covering faces)
- They become the story they're telling
- The DM's sacrifice at the end = leadership, legacy, letting go

---

# 2. MUSIC SELECTION & ARRANGEMENT

## Primary Repertoire

### Modest Mussorgsky / Maurice Ravel: Pictures at an Exhibition

**Movement 1: The Hut on Hen's Legs (Baba Yaga)**
- Duration: ~4-5 minutes (depending on tempo choices and transitions)
- Character: Dark, rhythmic, driving, chaotic
- Key moments:
  - Opening brass blast (corps assembles into square)
  - Percussive rhythmic section (battery feature)
  - Building intensity (vortex drill, Hut animation)
  - Natural lull (atmospheric percussion moment)

**Movement 2: The Great Gate of Kiev**
- Duration: ~4-5 minutes
- Character: 
  - Season: Triumphant, bright, traditional brass fanfare
  - Finals: Warm, enveloping, transcendent (mellophone-led)
- Key moments:
  - Opening fanfare (Season: trumpets; Finals: mellophones)
  - Building crescendo (stillness during Finals makes this FEEL bigger)
  - Climactic release (measures 43-50, brass facing audience)

### Optional: Phoenix Ostinato
- Subtle percussion overlay during Phoenix moment
- Drawn from Inferno (2018) percussion palette concept
- Tasteful, symbolic, not overpowering
- Adds textural depth without cluttering the arrangement

---

## Percussion Palette

### Battery
**Standard line:**
- Snares: ~8-10
- Tenors: ~5-6
- Bass drums: ~5-6
- Cymbals: ~4-5

**Baba Yaga Demands:**
- Rhythmic precision (driving ostinatos)
- Dynamic contrast (soft to loud builds)
- Textural variety (rim clicks, scrapes, dead sticking)

**Great Gate Demands:**
- Power and sustain (supporting brass wall)
- Rhythmic integrity during stillness (they keep playing while brass is motionless)

### Front Ensemble
**Instrumentation:**
- Marimbas: 2-3
- Vibraphones: 2
- Synthesizers: 2-3
- Glockenspiel, woodblocks, anvils, frame drums, shakers (Baba Yaga atmospheric moment)
- Timpani (optional, for Great Gate power)

**Baba Yaga Feature:**
- Glockenspiel (E♭ out-of-sync moment—Assistant's "warning")
- Woodblocks, anvils, shakers, frame drums (painting the inner world during the lull)

---

## Brass Arrangement Strategy

### Season Shows (Standard Voicing)
- Trumpets: Fanfare lines, melodic leads
- Mellophones: Harmonic support, counter-melodies
- Baritones: Inner voices, rhythmic support
- Tubas: Bass line, foundation

### Finals Show (Mellophone/Trumpet Swap)
**Great Gate of Kiev ONLY:**
- Mellophones: Play trumpet parts (take the heroic fanfare lines)
- Trumpets: Play mellophone parts (provide harmonic support)

**Why This Works:**
- **Timbral shift:** Warmth (mellophones) replaces brightness (trumpets)
- **Thematic resonance:** Arrival and homecoming, not conquest
- **Learning strategy:** Members absorb each other's parts organically all season (singing on the bus, noodling in warm-ups, passive listening)
- **Execution safety:** By Finals, both sections know both parts

---

## Music Licensing & Rights

**Public Domain Status:**
- Mussorgsky's original compositions: Public domain
- Ravel's orchestrations: Public domain in most jurisdictions (check specific territories)

**Arrangement Rights:**
- Academy will need to commission or license a brass/percussion arrangement
- Many DCI-specific arrangers are familiar with this repertoire
- Estimated cost: [To be determined by arranger—typically $3,000-$8,000 for full show]

---

# 3. CORPS CONFIGURATION & INSTRUMENTATION

## Standard DCI Configuration (Max 165 Members)

### Brass: 64 (8×8 Grid)
**Instrumentation:**
- Trumpets: 16 (2 rows of 8 in the grid)
- Mellophones: 16 (2 rows of 8 in the grid)
- Baritones: 16 (2 rows of 8 in the grid)
- Tubas: 16 (2 rows of 8 in the grid)

**Interwoven Pattern (Finals Only):**
- B–M–T–Tu repeating across the 8×8 formation
- Creates harmonic balance across the entire perimeter
- Every yard line has all four voices represented

### Battery: ~30
- Snares: 8-10
- Tenors: 5-6
- Bass drums: 5-6
- Cymbals: 4-5

### Front Ensemble: ~12
- Mallet percussion: 6-8
- Synthesizers/electronics: 2-3
- Auxiliary percussion: 2-3

### Color Guard: ~32
- Standard flags, rifles, sabres (as appropriate)
- Large Phoenix flag: requires 6-10 members to manipulate
- Costumes: Traditional glitter (season), Slavic-inspired layers (Finals reveal)

### Drum Major: 1
- Plus Assistant Drum Major for staging/Hut animation if needed

**TOTAL: ~139-153 members** (leaves room for Academy's actual corps size)

---

# 4. SEASON SHOW: COMPLETE BREAKDOWN

## Pre-Show (Standard Entry)

**Corps enters normally:**
- Marching in from the tunnel
- Standard pre-show formation or free-flow assembly

**Assembly:**
- Corps forms 8×8 square perimeter on the field
- 64 brass members position on the OUTLINE of the square (interior empty)
- Battery positions in the center (facing backfield initially)
- Guard spreads along outer edges
- Drum Major takes podium (standard position, front sideline or back sideline)

**Visual:**
- The square is the ritual boundary
- The empty interior = the unknown, the space of transformation
- Four corners remain anchored (always someone in those spots) throughout the show

---

## Movement I: Baba Yaga (The Trial)

### Opening (Measures 1-20)

**Music starts DURING announcement:**
- Battery begins Baba Yaga heartbeat cadence BEFORE announcer finishes
- This is unconventional—creates immediate unease
- Brass remains perfectly still (despite drums starting)
- Crowd feels tension building

**First brass blast:**
- Brass explodes into the opening fanfare
- Square perimeter holds (four corners anchored)
- Battery intensifies rhythm
- Guard begins slow, drifting movement along outer edges

---

### The Hut Appears (Measures 20-40)

**Prop Introduction:**
- The Hut (lightweight PVC + fabric structure) is brought onto the field
- Positioned near the back edge of the square or inside it
- Two performers (Baba Yaga + Assistant) enter the Hut
- Hut begins to twitch, shift, animate (Da Vinci walking machine concept)

**Visual Design:**
- The Hut is weird, unsettling, organic
- Moves in jerky, bird-like motions (hen's legs)
- Represents the unknown, the trial, the thing you must face

---

### Vortex Drill (Measures 40-80)

**Formation Changes:**
- Brass square perimeter remains INTACT (four corners always anchored)
- Brass members flow through curved, organic drill (Blue Knights style)
- Guard creates CLOCKWISE ring (outside or around the square)
- Battery creates COUNTERCLOCKWISE ring (inside the square)

**Rotating Vortex:**
- Two opposing rotations create visual chaos
- The Hut stands at the center or back, watching/looming
- Asymmetry, tension, constant motion

**Peak Chaos:**
- All elements moving simultaneously
- Drill reaches maximum demand and speed
- Hut fully animated, walking on stilt-legs (if mechanism allows)
- Sound builds to overwhelming intensity

---

### The Assistant's Escape Attempt (Measure 80-90)

**Key Moment:**
- Assistant figure (inside the Hut) tries to "warn the world"
- Plays E♭ on glockenspiel OUT OF SYNC with the ensemble
- Chaos intensifies briefly

**DM Descends:**
- Drum Major steps down from podium
- Walks deliberately toward the Assistant
- Guides her back into the ritual (visual: hand on shoulder, calm gesture)
- Assistant returns to the Hut
- "The Hut receives her"

**Thematic Meaning:**
- You cannot escape the trial by warning others
- You must face it yourself
- The guide (DM) ensures the crossing happens

---

### The Quiet Crisis (Measures 90-110)

**NOT a full stop, NOT silence:**
- This is the natural LULL in the brass texture (Mussorgsky wrote it this way)
- Brass drops to soft, sustained tones or rests
- Battery does NOT feature fully—this is front ensemble's moment

**Atmospheric Percussion:**
- Glockenspiel (E♭, now IN SYNC)
- Woodblocks (dry, clicking, like footsteps)
- Anvils (distant, metallic)
- Shakers, frame drums (textural whispers)

**Visual:**
- Drill slows, becomes more deliberate
- Guard performs quick-change (removes outer layer or adjusts costume to reveal layered design beneath—subtle)
- Hut stands still, leaning forward, looming

**Effect:**
- Eerie, introspective
- "What's inside the Hut?"
- Painting Baba Yaga's inner world without words

---

### Final Build (Measures 110-End of Baba Yaga)

**Brass returns:**
- Full power, driving rhythms
- Vortex drill intensifies one last time
- Hut walks/shifts aggressively
- Peak energy, overwhelming

**Transition Preparation:**
- Drill begins to resolve (slowing down, moving toward next formation)
- Energy peaks, then begins to drop
- Brass texture thins slightly
- Music approaches transition point to Great Gate

---

## Movement II: The Great Gate of Kiev (Season Version)

### Transition (Brief Pause or Underscoring)

**Season shows: Minimal pause (1-3 seconds max)**
- Just enough to shift energy from chaos to triumph
- Brass may hold a brief fermata or play transitional chord
- Drill shifts from vortex chaos to more traditional formations

---

### Opening Fanfare (Measures 1-20)

**Traditional Brass Voicing:**
- Trumpets play trumpet parts (bright, heroic fanfare)
- Mellophones play mellophone parts (harmonic support)

**Drill:**
- Traditional arcs, curves, dynamic staging
- Corps moves OUT of the square perimeter into flowing forms
- Guard flourishes (flag tosses, rifle work, dynamic movement)

**Visual:**
- This is the ARRIVAL moment
- Triumphant, joyful, traditional DCI aesthetic
- Crowd-pleasing, accessible

---

### Building Intensity (Measures 20-40)

**Drill continues:**
- Curved paths, company fronts, expanding/contracting forms
- Battery supports with powerful rhythmic hits
- Guard creates visual punctuation with equipment work

**Musical Build:**
- Dynamic crescendos
- Brass power increases
- Texture thickens

---

### The Phoenix Moment (Measure 40-50)

**Phoenix Flag Unfurls:**
- 60-yard silk flag begins at the BACK of the formation
- Guard team (6-10 members) unfurls it forward
- Flag travels OVER the brass, battery, and guard
- Collapses at the FRONT of the field (toward audience)

**Visual:**
- Massive, cinematic, overwhelming
- Colors: Red, orange, gold (fire, rebirth, transformation)
- The Phoenix is the visual climax of the season show

**DM retrieves [cultural element]:**
- After the Phoenix collapses, a small object (toy, prop, cultural symbol) is left behind
- DM walks to retrieve it

---

### Crowd Moment (Optional - Southwest Cultural Element)

**Options:**
1. **Coyote figure** (puppet, costume, or small prop)
   - Appears near the DM
   - Playful interaction (coyote "steals" the object, DM chases, lighthearted)
   - Coyote and DM exit together

2. **Roadrunner prop** (lightweight, stylized)
   - Similar playful interaction
   - Iconic Southwest imagery

3. **Dust devil visual** (silk, ribbons, spinning prop)
   - Guard creates a swirling visual
   - DM "releases" it, it dissipates
   - Metaphor: releasing chaos, embracing arrival

4. **No animal/element** (if Academy prefers simplicity)
   - DM simply retrieves object, holds it, exits with corps

**Effect:**
- Humanizing moment
- Accessible, warm, joyful
- Audience laughs, applauds
- Season show ends on a high, playful note

---

### Exit

**Corps exits toward tunnel:**
- Traditional exit formation (company front, two lines, or free-flow)
- DM exits with the corps
- Celebration, energy, joy

---

# 5. FINALS SHOW: TRANSFORMATION & CHANGES

## What Stays the SAME

**Critical: Minimize changes to reduce rehearsal burden and execution risk.**

**Unchanged Elements:**
- Baba Yaga drill (100% identical to season shows)
- Baba Yaga music (100% identical to season shows)
- Guard choreography during Great Gate (100% identical to season shows)
- Battery staging during Great Gate (100% identical to season shows)
- Phoenix flag unfurling (100% identical to season shows)

**The ONLY changes:**
1. 15-20 second transformation ritual (replaces brief season pause)
2. Brass stillness during Great Gate (replaces moving drill)
3. Mellophone/trumpet part swap (Great Gate only)
4. DM exit ritual (replaces playful crowd moment)

---

## Pre-Show (Finals Night Difference)

**Corps enters in whites (appears identical):**
- Same formation, same assembly
- Audience thinks: "This looks like every other show"

**Subtle 10-15 second delay:**
- After assembly, a brief pause (not long enough to be obvious, just... slightly off)
- Members turn to each other
- Whisper (barely audible, intimate): *"Tonight... the Gate is waiting..."*

**Then:**
- Announcer begins
- Battery interrupts with Baba Yaga heartbeat (same as all season)
- Show proceeds

---

## Movement I: Baba Yaga (Finals - IDENTICAL to Season)

**Everything proceeds exactly as in season shows:**
- Same drill
- Same music
- Same Hut animation
- Same vortex
- Same Assistant moment
- Same atmospheric percussion feature
- Same final build

**Corps is STILL in white jackets throughout Baba Yaga.**

**Audience thinks:** "Okay, this is the show we've seen all summer."

---

## THE TRANSFORMATION RITUAL (15-20 Seconds)

### When It Happens

**At the transition point between Baba Yaga and Great Gate:**
- Music STOPS (not a brief pause—a FULL STOP)
- All sound ceases
- Baba Yaga freezes (last image held)
- Hut leans forward (menacing or expectant)
- Brass turns inward (facing center) OR holds position

**This silence does NOT exist in season shows.**  
**Finals crowd immediately knows: something is different.**

---

### What Happens (Choreographed, Synchronized)

**Step 1: Drum Major Descends (3-5 seconds)**
- DM steps down from original podium
- Walks deliberately to center podium on 50-yard line
- (If podium needs to be moved into position, props crew does so during the silence—quick, efficient)
- DM ascends center podium
- **DM does NOT remove any uniform**—remains in full whites

**Step 2: The Corps Transforms (10-15 seconds)**
- In perfect unison, synchronized:
  1. Each brass member removes white jacket
  2. Folds or places it carefully
  3. Lays it to the RIGHT in a straight line (along the perimeter edge)
  4. Removes hat (shako)
  5. Places hat ON TOP of jacket
  6. Pulls earth-toned wrap/balaclava over face (or reveals earth-toned underlayer)

**Result:**
- 64 white jackets lined along the perimeter of the square
- 64 hats stacked on top
- 64 corps members in earth tones or black, faces covered or wrapped
- DM in full whites, elevated on center podium, UNCHANGED

**Visual:**
- The square perimeter is now outlined by WHITE (jackets/hats on the turf)
- The corps stands TRANSFORMED (color shifted, faces obscured)
- The DM is ISOLATED (the only one still in whites, still visible, still human)

---

### The Stillness (2-3 seconds)

**After transformation completes:**
- Pause
- Breath
- Silence

**Audience reaction:**
- Shock
- Recognition ("This is DIFFERENT")
- Anticipation ("What happens now?")

---

### Transition to Great Gate

**Music begins:**
- Mellophone opening fanfare (NOT trumpets—immediate sonic shift)
- Corps is already in 8×8 square perimeter (no drill movement needed)
- Brass faces CENTER (toward DM podium)
- Great Gate movement begins

---

## Movement II: The Great Gate of Kiev (Finals Version)

### The Formation

**8×8 Square Perimeter:**
- 64 brass members on the OUTLINE of the square
- Positioned on the 50-yard line, extending to ~30-yard lines on each side
- Facing CENTER (toward DM podium in the middle)
- **Interior is empty** except for:
  - DM podium (center)
  - Guard performing choreography
  - Battery performing (positioned inside or around)

**Jackets and Hats:**
- Remain on the turf, lining the outer edge of the square
- Visual boundary marker
- Memorial ground—"This is what we left behind to cross"

---

### Measures 1-42: The Stillness

**Brass:**
- MOTIONLESS
- Standing in perfect posture
- Facing center (toward DM)
- Playing at FULL POWER
- Zero drill demand

**Why This Works:**
- Focus shifts to SOUND (tone, blend, intonation)
- Judges cannot assess marching technique (there is none)
- But they MUST assess the BOLDNESS and DISCIPLINE of the choice
- The stillness makes the music FEEL bigger (no visual distraction)

**Guard & Battery:**
- Continue their normal choreography (same as season shows)
- They provide ALL the visual motion inside the frame
- Brass is the CONTAINER; guard/battery are the ACTION

**Mellophone/Trumpet Swap:**
- Mellophones playing trumpet parts = warmth, not brightness
- Audience hears the DIFFERENCE (even if they don't consciously know why)
- Judges recognize the RISK and CREATIVITY

**Interwoven Grid (B-M-T-Tu):**
- Every voice represented equally across the perimeter
- Creates a WALL OF SOUND
- Judges in the center hear unprecedented BLEND
- Individual caption judges struggle to isolate sections (slight score loss)
- Ensemble judges score SKY HIGH (blend is perfect)

---

### Measure 43: The Turn

**Brass begins to rotate:**
- Slow, synchronized turn
- All 64 members moving as ONE
- Facing CENTER → Facing AUDIENCE (front sideline)
- Takes approximately 8 measures to complete

**Visual Impact:**
- The frame OPENS
- What was facing inward now faces OUTWARD
- The Gate has turned to REVEAL what's inside
- Guard/battery inside are now FRAMED by the brass (from audience perspective)

**Sonic Impact:**
- Sound shifts from projecting CENTER (toward DM/judges) to projecting FORWARD (toward audience)
- Audience receives full sonic BLAST
- Judges behind the formation now hear reflected/ambient sound (quieter)

---

### Measures 43-50: The Final Release

**Brass facing audience:**
- Playing the climactic ending
- Still MOTIONLESS (except for the turn itself)
- Maximum power, maximum blend

**Phoenix Moment:**
- Same as season shows
- 60-yard flag unfurls from back, travels over formation, collapses at front
- Guard executes (same choreography)

**Handler Retrieves [Object]:**
- Handler (NOT DM) walks to front where Phoenix collapsed
- Retrieves [cultural element/toy/object] from the silk
- Walks back toward center field
- Places object near where DM will place hat (10-yard back hash? or center field?)
- **Hesitates (2-3 seconds—this is the KEY moment)**
- Picks object back up
- Carries it offstage toward props/pit truck

**Effect:**
- "Almost left it behind... but couldn't"
- Ambiguous: Is this HONORING the past? Or REFUSING to let go?
- Audience projects their own meaning

---

### The Exit Formation

**Corps condenses:**
- From 8×8 square perimeter into TWO LINES of 32 each
- Formation moves toward back hash (toward tunnel/exit)

**Drum Major joins:**
- Steps down from center podium
- Joins at the FRONT CORNER of the formation
- **65 total members** (64 + DM = odd number, asymmetrical, visually striking)

**March Tempo:**
- **Corps:** Normal marching tempo (standard cadence)
- **Drum Major:** 7/4 time (slower, deliberate, OUT OF SYNC)

**Visual:**
- Corps flows forward (steady, unified)
- DM lags behind (moving through different TIME)
- Together but separate

---

### The Drum Major's Final Moment

**DM stops at 10-yard back hash:**
- Corps KEEPS MARCHING (doesn't stop, doesn't look back)
- DM stands ALONE
- Silence (or just the sound of corps exiting in the distance)

**The Salute:**
- Full, proper drum major salute
- NOT a military salute—a DRUM MAJOR salute (the perfected one)
- Held for 2-3 seconds
- **This is the FIRST TIME the audience sees the complete, perfect salute**
- All season, the opening salute was short/stylized ("still learning")
- THIS is mastery

**The Hat:**
- DM removes hat (drum major cover)
- Holds it for a moment (weight, reverence)
- Places it on the ground at the 10-yard line
- The hat STAYS

**About-Face:**
- Crisp, military-precise turn
- DM now faces away from the audience (toward the tunnel)

**March Off:**
- DM marches alone
- In 7/4 time? Or returns to normal tempo? (Designer's choice)
- Walks into the tunnel
- Disappears

**Final Image:**
- Hat alone on the 10-yard back hash
- Silence
- Then: **ERUPTION from the tunnel** (corps celebrating, welcoming DM back)

**Audience hears the celebration but cannot SEE it.**

---

# 6. VISUAL DESIGN & FORMATIONS

## Core Formation: The 8×8 Square Perimeter

**Why a Square?**
- Geometric clarity (easy to see, easy to judge)
- Ritual boundary (frames the action inside)
- Symbolic container (the space where transformation happens)
- Four corners = stability, constancy (always anchored)

**Dimensions:**
- 64 brass members forming the OUTLINE (not a block—just the perimeter)
- Approximately 30-yard span (from 25-yard line to 25-yard line, or similar)
- Centered on 50-yard line (for Finals Great Gate moment)

**Interior:**
- EMPTY of brass (brass is on the perimeter only)
- Guard performs inside
- Battery performs inside
- DM podium inside (Finals: on the 50, center of square)

---

## Baba Yaga Drill Design Principles

**Flowing, Curved Paths:**
- Blue Knights-style musicality (not rigid straight lines)
- Organic, asymmetrical movement
- Constant motion, never static (except opening/transition moments)

**Four Corners Anchored:**
- Always someone in the four corner positions of the square
- Even as drill flows and shifts, corners remain reference points
- Provides visual stability amidst chaos

**Vortex/Rotating Rings:**
- Guard: Clockwise rotation (outside or around the square)
- Battery: Counterclockwise rotation (inside the square)
- Creates opposing motion, visual tension

**Demand Scaling:**
- Early season: Simpler curves, wider spacing (forgiving)
- Late season: Tighter spacing, faster tempo (as execution improves)

---

## Great Gate Drill Design Principles

**Season:**
- Traditional DCI drill (arcs, company fronts, dynamic forms)
- High visual demand (moving drill, spacing changes, tempo)
- Crowd-pleasing, accessible

**Finals:**
- 8×8 square perimeter, MOTIONLESS (measures 1-42)
- The Turn (measures 43-50, slow synchronized rotation)
- ZERO drill demand during stillness = MAXIMUM execution safety

---

## Spacing & Alignment

**Square Perimeter Spacing:**
- 16 members per side (if perfect square: 4 members per corner edge, 8 per straight edge)
- OR: distribute 64 members evenly around the perimeter (precise spacing TBD in drill design phase)

**Interwoven Grid (Finals, B-M-T-Tu):**
- Baritone, Mellophone, Trumpet, Tuba repeating around the perimeter
- Every 4th person is the same instrument
- Creates harmonic balance across the formation

---

# 7. PROPS & STAGING ELEMENTS

## The Hut (Baba Yaga's Dwelling)

**Design Concept:**
- Lightweight, portable structure
- Represents Baba Yaga's mobile home (hut on hen's legs)
- Weird, organic, unsettling aesthetic

**Materials:**
- **Frame:** PVC piping (lightweight, durable, easy to transport)
- **Covering:** Fabric (canvas, muslin, or synthetic—earth tones, textured, aged look)
- **Mechanism:** Da Vinci walking machine concept (two performers inside animate the legs)

**Size:**
- Approximately 6-8 feet tall (when upright)
- 4-6 feet wide
- Collapsible for transport

**Animation:**
- **Season shows:** Mostly low to ground, twitching, shifting
- **Finals:** Stands fully upright on stilt-legs (performers inside walk it)

**Prototype Opportunity:**
- Can be built and tested in Albuquerque with local creative team
- Video proof-of-concept provided to Academy before commitment

**Estimated Cost:** $500-$1,200 (materials + local labor)

---

## The Phoenix Flag

**Design Concept:**
- Massive silk flag representing rebirth, transformation, fire
- Unfurls from back of formation, travels over corps, collapses at front

**Dimensions:**
- **60 yards wide** (full span across the field)
- Height: 10-15 feet (when fully extended vertically)

**Colors:**
- Red, orange, gold gradient (fire, warmth, rebirth)
- OR: Earth tones (rust, ochre, clay—if Southwest aesthetic preferred)

**Materials:**
- Lightweight silk or synthetic silk (durable, flows well, packs small)
- Weighted edges (subtle weights sewn into hem for controlled travel)

**Manipulation:**
- Requires 6-10 guard members to unfurl and control
- Choreographed release, travel, and collapse

**Prototype Opportunity:**
- Half-scale version (30 yards) can be built and tested in Albuquerque
- Validates unfurling mechanics, travel distance, collapse control

**Estimated Cost:** $800-$1,500 (materials + construction)

---

## Drum Major Podium(s)

**Season Shows:**
- Standard DM podium (front sideline or back sideline, per Academy's usual setup)

**Finals:**
- **Center podium** added on 50-yard line (inside the square)
- 2'×2' platform, 6-12" elevation (just enough to be visible, not towering)
- Portable, lightweight (props crew moves into position during 15-20 second silence)

**Estimated Cost:** $200-$400 (if building new; may already exist in Academy's inventory)

---

## Jackets & Hats (Left on Field)

**Not props—actual uniform pieces:**
- 64 white jackets (what members are wearing)
- 64 shakos/hats (what members are wearing)

**Staging:**
- Removed during transformation ritual
- Placed on turf in straight lines along square perimeter
- Left on field during Great Gate (visual boundary marker)
- Retrieved by props crew after show OR members pick them up during exit (design choice)

**No additional cost** (these are existing uniform pieces)

---

# 8. COSTUMES & UNIFORM DESIGN

## Season Shows: Traditional Whites

**Brass & Battery:**
- White jackets (standard DCI formal)
- Black pants
- Black shoes
- Gloves (black or white, per Academy preference)

**Purpose:**
- Clean, professional, traditional DCI aesthetic
- High contrast (white tops, black bottoms)
- Hides lower body imperfections (footwork less visible)

---

## Finals Show: Transformation Reveal

**Brass & Battery:**
- **UNDER the white jackets (hidden all season):**
  - Black or earth-toned long-sleeve athletic shirts (lightweight, moisture-wicking)
  - OR: Earth-toned layers (rust, ochre, sand, clay—Southwest palette)
- **Face coverings (Finals only):**
  - Earth-toned wraps/balaclavas (pulled from pocket/belt during transformation)
  - OR: Black balaclavas (if going for starker aesthetic)

**Drum Major:**
- **Does NOT transform**
- Remains in full white jacket, hat, traditional uniform
- Visual isolation: DM is the only one still "human," still visible

---

## Color Guard Costumes

**Season Shows:**
- Traditional glitter guard aesthetic
- Bright, colorful, eye-catching
- Standard DCI guard look

**Finals Transformation:**
- **Layered costume design:**
  - Glitter costume is OUTER layer
  - Slavic-inspired or Southwest-inspired tunic/layers HIDDEN beneath
- **Quick-change during Baba Yaga atmospheric moment:**
  - Outer layer removed or adjusted (subtle, not flashy)
  - Reveals earth-toned, textured, frostwoven-style layers beneath
- **Effect:** Guard transforms from bright/modern to mythic/ancient

**Prototype Opportunity:**
- Costume designer (burlesque performer with quick-change expertise) in Albuquerque
- Can design and build prototype to test quick-change speed and visual impact

**Estimated Cost:** $150-$300 per guard member × 32 = $4,800-$9,600 total

---

# 9. REHEARSAL STRATEGY & MEMBER DEVELOPMENT

## Brass: Mellophone/Trumpet Part Learning

**The Strategy: Passive Organic Learning**

**Throughout the Season (May-August):**
- Members learn their ASSIGNED parts (trumpets learn trumpet, mellos learn mello)
- BUT: Staff subtly encourages cross-section familiarity:
  - "Trumpets, can you sing the mello line here? Just for blend."
  - "Mellos, hum the trumpet fanfare—let's hear how it fits."
  - "Everyone, let's ghost the other section's part quietly during this rep."

**In the Lot, On the Bus, In Free Time:**
- Members naturally noodle, sing, absorb each other's parts
- By July, both sections have PASSIVELY learned both parts
- No formal "sit down and learn the swap" rehearsal needed

**Finals Week:**
- Staff announces: "For Finals, trumpets play mello parts, mellos play trumpet parts."
- Members: "Wait, we already KNOW these parts."
- Staff: "Exactly. Now let's just clean the balance."
- **Result:** Minimal rehearsal time, high confidence, clean execution

---

## Visual: Stillness Discipline

**The Challenge:**
- Standing motionless for 42 measures is HARDER than it sounds
- Any drift, wobble, or posture collapse is VISIBLE
- Judges will notice

**The Strategy:**

**Early Season (May-June):**
- Drill the square perimeter formation repeatedly
- Focus on: spacing, alignment, posture
- Hold for 10 seconds, 20 seconds, 30 seconds (building endurance)

**Mid-Season (July):**
- Add PLAYING while motionless (breath control, embouchure stability)
- Focus on: no swaying, no rocking, no shifting weight
- Mental discipline: "You are a pillar. You are the Gate."

**Late Season (August, Finals Prep):**
- Full run-throughs of 42-measure stillness
- Video review: check for ANY drift or movement
- Refinement: micro-adjustments to posture, spacing

**Mental Preparation:**
- "This isn't about NOT moving. It's about PRESENCE."
- "You are the threshold. You hold the space. You ARE the Gate."

---

## Guard & Battery: No Changes

**Advantage:**
- Guard learns ONE show, performs it all season
- Battery learns ONE show, performs it all season
- Finals = ZERO new choreography for them
- Focus: cleaning what they already know, not learning new material

---

## Drum Major: Salute Progression

**The Arc:**

**Season Shows (Opening):**
- Short, stylized salute (functional but not ceremonial)
- Suggests: "I'm still learning this. I'm still becoming."

**Finals (Closing):**
- FULL, proper drum major salute (textbook perfect)
- This is the FIRST TIME the audience sees the complete version
- Payoff: "I've been practicing all summer. This is mastery."

**Rehearsal:**
- DM works on the "perfect salute" privately all season
- Staff gives feedback, refinement
- Finals = debut of the completed skill

---

# 10. SCORING ANALYSIS & COMPETITIVE POSITIONING

## Predicted Caption Scores (Finals, First Year)

### Music Achievement: 19.3-19.6 / 20

**Brass Achievement: 9.7-9.85 / 10**
- Strengths: Stillness allows focus on tone/blend, mello/trumpet swap showcases versatility
- Weaknesses: Individual judges can't isolate sections (potential -0.3 to -0.5)

**Percussion Achievement: 9.6-9.75 / 10**
- Strengths: Battery has full demand, rhythmic integrity maintained
- Weaknesses: Judge can't hear battery clearly during brass stillness (potential -0.2 to -0.3)

---

### Music Effect: 19.8-20 / 20

**Strengths:**
- Sonic wall during stillness = unprecedented
- Directional staging (brass facing center, then audience)
- Mello/trumpet swap = warmth and creativity
- 15-20 second silence = bold storytelling

**Weaknesses:** None (this is where the show DOMINATES)

---

### Visual Achievement: 18.5-19 / 20

**Marching: 9.0-9.3 / 10**
- Strengths: Stillness executed perfectly, turn is clean, Baba Yaga drill is solid
- Weaknesses: Stillness = minimal demand (-0.5 to -1 point potential loss)

**Guard: 9.5-9.7 / 10**
- Strengths: Phoenix flag, costume transformation, choreography inside square
- Weaknesses: Judge has trouble tracking due to brass perimeter blocking sightlines (-0.2 to -0.3)

---

### Visual Effect: 19.8-20 / 20

**Strengths:**
- Transformation ritual = iconic
- Stillness = bold visual statement
- The turn = dramatic shift
- DM exit = devastating
- Hat left on field = unforgettable image

**Weaknesses:** None (GE GOLD)

---

### General Effect Music: 9.8-10 / 10

**Strengths:**
- Clear narrative arc (trial → crossing → arrival)
- Musical storytelling is tight
- Mello/trumpet swap serves the story
- Silence = emotional weight
- DM exit in 7/4 = final punctuation

---

### General Effect Visual: 9.9-10 / 10

**Strengths:**
- Transformation happens in front of the audience (they witness it)
- Square as ritual frame = thematically perfect
- DM's sacrifice = devastating
- Hat as final image = poetry
- Dual-version structure = design mastery

---

## Total Predicted Score (Year 1)

**Conservative:** 95.0 (clean execution, judges slightly skeptical)  
**Likely:** 95.5-96.5 (clean execution, judges reward boldness)  
**Best Case:** 97.0 (flawless execution, judges lose their minds)

---

6. Blue Knights: 94.988

**If Academy scores 97.0:**

### Year 2 (Refined Execution):

**Predicted Score:** 96.5-97.5

**Impact:** Academy becomes a household name, recruiting skyrockets, legacy established

---

## Risk Assessment

### Execution Risks (Year 1):
- Stillness has drift (brass shifts position slightly)
- Phoenix flag tangles or doesn't unfurl cleanly
- Mello/trumpet swap has intonation issues
- DM exit timing is rushed

**Mitigation:**
- Drill stillness obsessively (video review, micro-adjustments)
- Test Phoenix flag repeatedly (prototype first)
- Trust organic learning strategy for part swap
- Rehearse DM exit timing separately

---

### Judging Risks:
- Individual brass judges penalize inability to isolate sections
- Visual Performance judge penalizes lack of demand during stillness
- Judges don't "get" the boldness, score it as gimmicky

**Mitigation:**
- Accept that individual captions may score slightly lower
- Trust that Effect and GE scores compensate (and then some)
- Design intent must be CLEAR (not confusing or ambiguous)

---

## Why This Show Scores 96-97 (Realistic)

**Loss:** ~2-3 points (individual brass, marching demand)  
**Gain:** ~5-8 points (ensemble, effect, GE)  
**Net:** +3 to 5 points over a "traditional" show

**Result:** Academy leaps from 91.5 (16th) to 95-97 (Top 6 or Top 3)

# 1. OVERVIEW & DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

## Design Principles

All props and costumes for "The Gate" are designed with three core principles:

**1. Portability**
- Must pack efficiently for tour (truck space is limited)
- Lightweight materials that don't sacrifice visual impact
- Collapsible/modular designs where possible

**2. Durability**
- Must survive 15-20 performances plus rehearsals
- Weather-resistant (summer heat, occasional rain)
- Repairable in the field if damaged

**3. Cost-Efficiency**
- Academy-appropriate budget (not BD/Crown-level resources)
- Local sourcing where possible (Albuquerque creative network)
- Prototype-first approach (test before committing to full-scale production)

---

## Southwest Aesthetic (Academy-Specific)

Where appropriate, props and costumes incorporate Southwest/desert imagery:
- Earth tones (rust, ochre, sand, clay, terracotta)
- Textured fabrics (woven, layered, aged appearance)
- Cultural motifs (geometric patterns, natural materials)

This differentiates the Academy version from the Blue Knights version (which uses stark white/black contrast and Denver-specific elements).

---

# 2. THE HUT (Baba Yaga's Dwelling)

## Concept

A lightweight, portable structure representing Baba Yaga's mythical mobile home. The Hut is:
- Weird and unsettling (not cute or cartoonish)
- Organic and asymmetrical (feels alive, not mechanical)
- Animatable by performers (twitches, shifts, walks on stilt-legs)

---

## Design Specifications

### Structure
**Frame:**
- Material: Schedule 40 PVC piping (1" or 1.25" diameter)
- Joints: PVC connectors and tees (allows for quick assembly/disassembly)
- Reinforcement: Metal brackets at key stress points (corners, leg joints)

**Dimensions:**
- Height: 6-8 feet (when upright on legs)
- Width: 4-6 feet
- Depth: 4-5 feet
- Weight: 30-50 lbs (two performers can carry/manipulate comfortably)

### Covering
**Material Options:**
- Canvas duck cloth (durable, paintable, affordable)
- Muslin (lightweight, drapes well, less durable)
- Synthetic ripstop (weather-resistant, lightweight, more expensive)

**Color/Texture:**
- Earth tones: Browns, grays, rust, ochre
- Aged/weathered appearance (painted, distressed)
- Asymmetrical patches or layers (organic, not uniform)

**Attachment:**
- Velcro strips (allows for quick removal/replacement if damaged)
- Grommets and bungee cords (at key points for tension)

### "Hen's Legs" Mechanism
**Season Shows (Low Animation):**
- Hut sits low to ground on short legs (12-18" stilts or supports)
- Two performers inside shift weight to create twitching/rocking motion
- Legs can be simple PVC extensions with rubber feet

**Finals Show (Full Walking Animation):**
- Hut stands on 3-4 foot stilt-legs
- Performers inside use extended handles/grips to "walk" the Hut
- Inspired by Da Vinci walking machine concept
- Legs articulate at joints (knee-like bends for realistic gait)

**Mechanism Details:**
- Legs: Additional PVC extensions that telescope or lock into place
- Foot pads: Wide rubber or foam pads (prevent sinking into turf)
- Internal harness: Straps/handles for performers to control movement
- Practice required: 5-10 hours of rehearsal for smooth walking motion

---

## Prototype Plan

### Phase 1: Small-Scale Model (1:4 scale)
- **Purpose:** Test structural integrity, joint stability, covering attachment
- **Timeline:** 2-3 weeks
- **Cost:** $50-$100 (materials only)

### Phase 2: Full-Scale Non-Animated Version
- **Purpose:** Test size, weight, portability, visual impact from stands
- **Timeline:** 3-4 weeks
- **Cost:** $300-$500 (materials + labor)

### Phase 3: Full-Scale Animated Version (Walking Legs)
- **Purpose:** Test stilt-leg mechanism, performer control, walking motion
- **Timeline:** 4-6 weeks (includes performer training)
- **Cost:** $600-$900 (materials + labor + mechanism development)

**Total Prototype Investment:** $950-$1,500

---

## Production Costs (Final Version for Academy)

### Materials:
- PVC piping and connectors: $150-$200
- Canvas/fabric covering: $100-$150
- Paint, distressing materials: $50-$75
- Stilt-leg mechanism (Finals version): $100-$150
- Reinforcement hardware: $50-$75

### Labor:
- Design and fabrication: $300-$500 (local Albuquerque sculptor/builder)
- Painting/finishing: $100-$150

**Total Hut Cost:** $850-$1,300

---

## Transport & Storage

**Disassembled:**
- Frame: PVC pieces nest inside each other (4-5 foot bundle)
- Covering: Folds flat (2'×3' rolled bundle)
- Legs: Separate bundle (4-5 feet long)
- Total volume: ~3 cubic feet

**Assembly Time:** 10-15 minutes (two people, no tools required if designed with quick-connect joints)

---

## Visual Reference Concepts

*(In a formal pitch, this section would include sketches, renderings, or reference photos. For this document, descriptions are provided.)*

**Inspiration Images:**
- Hayao Miyazaki's "Howl's Moving Castle" (ramshackle, asymmetrical structure)
- Traditional Russian Baba Yaga hut illustrations (chicken-leg stilts)
- Burning Man kinetic sculptures (organic movement, PVC framework)

**Color Palette:**
- Primary: Weathered wood brown, gray-brown
- Accents: Rust, ochre, dark green (moss/lichen effect)
- Avoid: Bright colors, cartoon aesthetics

---

# 3. THE PHOENIX FLAG

## Concept

A massive silk flag representing transformation, rebirth, and fire. The Phoenix:
- Unfurls from the back of the formation
- Travels over the entire corps (brass, guard, battery)
- Collapses at the front (toward the audience)
- Symbolizes the crossing, the moment of emergence

---

## Design Specifications

### Dimensions
**Full-Scale (Performance):**
- Width: 60 yards (180 feet)
- Height (when extended vertically): 10-15 feet
- Total fabric area: ~1,800-2,700 square feet

**Half-Scale (Prototype/Testing):**
- Width: 30 yards (90 feet)
- Height: 8-10 feet
- Purpose: Validate mechanics, test weight/flow before full-scale production

### Material
**Fabric:**
- Lightweight silk or silk-like synthetic (China silk, habotai, or polyester imitation)
- Weight: 2-3 oz per square yard (light enough to flow, heavy enough to control)
- Finish: Matte or semi-gloss (not shiny—too theatrical)

**Color Options:**

**Option 1: Traditional Fire (Red/Orange/Gold)**
- Gradient from deep red (back edge) to orange (middle) to gold (front edge)
- Evokes flames, heat, rebirth through fire

**Option 2: Southwest Earth Tones (Rust/Ochre/Clay)**
- Gradient from rust (back) to ochre (middle) to sandy clay (front)
- Evokes desert sunrise, transformation through earth and heat
- More regionally appropriate for Academy

**Dyeing:**
- Hand-dyed or digitally printed (digital = more control, higher cost)
- Gradient must be smooth, not abrupt color blocks

### Edge Treatment
**Weighted Hem:**
- Thin metal chain or beaded cord sewn into bottom hem
- Weight: Just enough to control descent, not drag
- Purpose: Ensures flag collapses cleanly (doesn't billow upward)

**Top Edge (Release Point):**
- Reinforced hem with loops or grommets
- Attached to release mechanism (see below)

---

## Manipulation & Choreography

### Guard Team
**Personnel:** 6-10 guard members
- 2-3 at back edge (control release and initial unfurling)
- 3-5 along sides (guide the travel)
- 1-2 at front (control collapse and gather)

### Unfurling Sequence
1. **Release (Back Edge):**
   - Flag is bundled/rolled at back of formation
   - On cue, guard members release the top edge
   - Fabric begins to unfurl upward and forward

2. **Travel (Over the Corps):**
   - Flag is lifted and carried forward by guard members
   - Travels over brass perimeter (10-15 feet above heads)
   - Silk flows and undulates (creates visual wave effect)

3. **Collapse (Front Edge):**
   - Guard members at front allow flag to descend
   - Weighted hem pulls fabric down gently
   - Flag pools on the turf at the front of the field
   - [Cultural element/toy/object] is revealed in the fabric

### Timing
- Total sequence: 15-25 seconds (depending on tempo and formation size)
- Requires precise guard timing (release → travel → collapse must be synchronized)

---

## Prototype Plan

### Phase 1: Quarter-Scale Model (15 yards)
- **Purpose:** Test fabric weight, flow, color gradient
- **Timeline:** 1-2 weeks
- **Cost:** $100-$200

### Phase 2: Half-Scale Model (30 yards)
- **Purpose:** Test full unfurling mechanics, guard manipulation, collapse control
- **Timeline:** 3-4 weeks
- **Cost:** $400-$700

### Phase 3: Full-Scale Flag (60 yards)
- **Purpose:** Final production version
- **Timeline:** 4-6 weeks (includes dyeing/printing time)
- **Cost:** $800-$1,500 (see below)

**Total Prototype Investment:** $500-$900 (quarter + half scale)

---

## Production Costs (Final Version for Academy)

### Materials:
- Silk/silk-like fabric (1,800-2,700 sq ft): $400-$800
- Dyeing or digital printing: $200-$400
- Weighted hem (chain/beading): $50-$100
- Edge reinforcement (grommets, hem tape): $30-$50

### Labor:
- Sewing and finishing: $150-$250 (local seamstress/fabric artist)

**Total Phoenix Flag Cost:** $830-$1,600

---

## Transport & Storage

**Rolled:**
- Diameter: 8-12 inches
- Length: 10-15 feet (if rolled lengthwise)
- OR: Folded accordion-style into a 3'×3'×1' bundle

**Storage Considerations:**
- Must be kept dry (moisture = mildew)
- Stored in breathable bag (not plastic—needs air circulation)
- Takes up ~2-3 cubic feet in truck

---

## Visual Reference Concepts

**Inspiration Images:**
- Large silk flags used in Cirque du Soleil productions
- Parachute-style flags in Olympic ceremonies
- Color guard silks from Winter Guard International (WGI) shows

**Color Palette:**
- Option 1 (Fire): Deep crimson → burnt orange → golden yellow
- Option 2 (Earth): Rust red → terracotta → sandy ochre

---

# 4. DRUM MAJOR PODIUM (Center - Finals Only)

## Concept

A small, portable podium positioned at the center of the 8×8 square formation during the Finals version of "The Great Gate of Kiev." The DM conducts from this elevated position (inside the Gate) during the stillness and turn.

---

## Design Specifications

### Dimensions
- Platform: 2' × 2' (24" × 24")
- Height: 6-12 inches (just enough to elevate DM slightly above corps, not towering)
- Weight: 15-25 lbs (two people can carry easily)

### Materials
**Frame:**
- Aluminum or PVC (lightweight, rigid)
- Folding legs OR fixed legs with quick-connect joints

**Platform Surface:**
- Plywood (¾" thick) with non-slip surface (rubber mat or grip tape)
- Painted black or dark gray (low visibility from stands)

### Stability
- Wide base (prevents tipping)
- Rubber feet (grips turf, doesn't slide)
- Optional: Sandbag or weight at base for windy conditions

---

## Logistics

**Placement:**
- Carried onto field by props crew during the 15-20 second transformation silence
- Positioned at center of 50-yard line (inside the square)
- Takes 5-10 seconds to set in place

**Removal:**
- Carried off by props crew after DM descends for exit sequence
- OR: Left on field until after show ends (if not visually distracting)

---

## Production Costs

### Materials:
- Aluminum frame or PVC legs: $50-$75
- Plywood platform: $25-$40
- Non-slip surface: $15-$25
- Hardware (bolts, connectors): $10-$20

### Labor:
- Fabrication: $50-$100 (simple build, can be DIY)

**Total Podium Cost:** $150-$260

*(Note: Academy may already have a portable podium in inventory—check before building new)*

---

# 5. COLOR GUARD COSTUMES

## Concept

Guard costumes transform from traditional DCI glitter aesthetic (season shows) to Southwest-inspired mythic layers (Finals reveal). The transformation happens during the Baba Yaga atmospheric percussion moment via quick-change.

---

## Design Specifications

### Season Shows: Traditional Glitter Guard

**Outer Layer (Visible All Season):**
- Bodysuit or dress in Academy's colors (black/gold/maroon/etc.)
- Sequins, rhinestones, metallic fabrics (standard DCI guard aesthetic)
- Allows full range of motion (tosses, spins, dance)

**Purpose:**
- Accessible, crowd-pleasing, traditional
- Audience expects this—no surprises yet

---

### Finals Show: Layered Transformation

**Hidden Beneath (Revealed at Finals):**
- Earth-toned tunic or layered vest
- Colors: Rust, ochre, sand, clay, terracotta, burnt orange
- Textures: Woven, textured, aged appearance (NOT shiny or new-looking)
- Inspired by Southwest Native American aesthetics (with cultural respect—avoid direct appropriation, use general earth-tone aesthetic)

**Quick-Change Mechanism:**
- Outer glitter layer attached with velcro, snaps, or magnetic closures
- Removed or opened during the Baba Yaga atmospheric percussion lull (15-20 seconds)
- Guard members can execute the change while moving or in a brief hold

**Design Details:**
- Tunic: Sleeveless or short-sleeved (allows freedom of movement)
- Length: Hip-length or mid-thigh (practical for guard work)
- Embellishments: Minimal (subtle geometric patterns, fringe, natural fibers)

---

## Prototype Plan

### Phase 1: Single Costume Prototype
- **Purpose:** Test layering, quick-change speed, visual impact, range of motion
- **Timeline:** 2-3 weeks
- **Cost:** $150-$250

### Phase 2: Five-Costume Sample Set
- **Purpose:** Test color consistency, fabric durability, group visual effect
- **Timeline:** 3-4 weeks
- **Cost:** $750-$1,250 (5 × $150-$250)

**Total Prototype Investment:** $900-$1,500

---

## Production Costs (Final Version for Academy)

### Per-Costume Cost:
**Materials:**
- Outer glitter layer: $50-$80 (bodysuit, sequins, trim)
- Inner earth-tone tunic: $40-$70 (fabric, construction)
- Fasteners (velcro, snaps): $5-$10

**Labor:**
- Construction and fitting: $60-$90 (per costume, local seamstress)

**Total per costume:** $155-$250

**Total for 32 guard members:** $4,960-$8,000

---

## Sizing & Fitting

**Custom vs. Stock:**
- Custom-fit: More expensive, better fit, longer lead time
- Stock sizes with alterations: More affordable, faster turnaround

**Recommendation:** Stock sizes for outer layer (glitter), custom for inner layer (earth-tone tunic—simpler construction, easier to customize)

---

## Visual Reference Concepts

**Inspiration Images:**
- WGI (Winter Guard International) costume designs (layered, theatrical)
- Southwest textile patterns (Navajo, Hopi geometric designs—used respectfully)
- Festival/ceremonial garments (earth tones, natural fibers, woven textures)

**Color Palette:**
- Rust, terracotta, burnt sienna, ochre, sandy beige, clay
- Avoid: Bright turquoise, neon colors (not period/region appropriate)

---

---

## Why This Matters for "The Gate"

**"The Gate" is not a typical DCI show.**

It requires:
- **Discipline:** 42 measures of brass stillness with zero drift
- **Precision:** Synchronized jacket/hat removal during 15-20 second silence
- **Boldness:** Committing to unconventional staging choices
- **Trust:** Members must believe the stillness is MORE powerful than motion

**These are not things you can achieve through drill books alone.**

They require:
- Hands-on instruction
- Mental preparation
- Constant refinement
- A partner who understands BOTH the design intent AND the execution challenges

**That's what I'm offering.**

---

# 2. THE CHALLENGE: EXECUTING "THE GATE"

## What Makes This Show Difficult

### Challenge 1: The Stillness (42 Measures, Great Gate of Kiev)

**Why it's hard:**
- Standing motionless while playing = harder than it sounds
- Any drift, wobble, or posture collapse is VISIBLE
- Judges will notice even minor imperfections
- Members must trust that stillness = impact (not boring)

**What's required:**
- Drilling perfect spacing and alignment (no drift)
- Building postural endurance (42 measures is LONG)
- Teaching breath control (playing without swaying/rocking)
- Mental discipline: "You are the Gate. You hold the space."

---

### Challenge 2: The Transformation Ritual (15-20 Seconds)

**Why it's hard:**
- Must be SYNCHRONIZED (64 brass members removing jackets/hats in unison)
- Must be CLEAN (no fumbling, no dropped items)
- Must be DELIBERATE (not rushed—this is a ritual, not a costume change)
- Members must commit to the THEATRICALITY (this is a performance moment)

**What's required:**
- Rehearsing the choreography separately (outside of full run-throughs)
- Teaching placement precision (jackets/hats in straight lines)
- Building muscle memory (members can do this in their sleep)
- Mental preparation: "This is not weird. This is sacred."

---

### Challenge 3: The Interwoven Brass Grid (B-M-T-Tu Pattern)

**Why it's hard:**
- Members are NOT standing next to their section
- Traditional sectional balance doesn't work (you're surrounded by different voices)
- Intonation adjustments needed (you're hearing different intervals than usual)
- Individual errors are MORE exposed (no section to hide behind)

**What's required:**
- Teaching ensemble LISTENING (not just section listening)
- Drilling spacing with precision (interwoven pattern must be exact)
- Building confidence (members trust their neighbors even if they're different instruments)

---

### Challenge 4: Flowing Drill During Baba Yaga

**Why it's hard:**
- Blue Knights-style curved paths (not rigid straight lines)
- Vortex patterns with opposing rotations (guard clockwise, battery counterclockwise)
- High demand while maintaining the square perimeter anchor points
- Must look ORGANIC and MUSICAL (not robotic)

**What's required:**
- Teaching the FEEL of curved drill (not just hitting dots)
- Cleaning transitions between formations
- Building spatial awareness (knowing where you are in the vortex)
- Emphasizing musicality: "Move with the phrase, not against it"

---

## What Happens Without Proper Instruction

**If the stillness isn't drilled obsessively:**
- Drift happens (spacing changes, alignment breaks)
- Posture collapses (shoulders sag, instruments droop)
- Judges penalize execution

**If the transformation isn't rehearsed properly:**
- Members fumble jackets/hats (looks messy)
- Timing is off (not synchronized)
- Theatricality is lost (feels like a costume change, not a ritual)

**If the interwoven grid isn't taught carefully:**
- Blend suffers (members can't hear each other properly)
- Intonation issues arise (intervals are different than usual)
- Confidence drops (members feel isolated)

**If the Baba Yaga drill isn't cleaned thoroughly:**
- Curves look stiff (not organic)
- Vortex patterns lose clarity
- Musicality is lost (drill feels mechanical)

**Result:** A bold show concept undermined by execution flaws. Scores in the 93-94 range instead of 95-97.

---

# 3. SERVICES OFFERED

## What I'm Proposing

I'm offering a **full-season partnership** with The Academy to ensure "The Gate" is executed at the highest level possible.

---

## Service Package: Drill Design & Instruction

### Phase 1: Pre-Season (January-May 2026)

**Drill Design Collaboration:**
- Work with Academy's visual staff to write or refine drill for both Baba Yaga and Great Gate movements
- Provide input on formation transitions, spacing, and demand scaling
- Design the stillness formation (8×8 square perimeter with interwoven grid)
- Choreograph the transformation ritual (jacket/hat removal sequence)

**Deliverables:**
- Drill coordinates (if writing from scratch)
- Drill refinements (if collaborating with existing staff designer)
- Transformation ritual choreography notes
- Stillness formation spacing chart

**Time Commitment:** 20-30 hours (remote, via video calls and shared documents)

---

### Phase 2: Spring Training Camp (June 2026)

**On-Site Instruction (5-7 Days):**

**Focus Areas:**
1. **Teach the Square Perimeter Formation**
   - Drill spacing and alignment
   - Teach the four corner anchor points
   - Introduce the interwoven grid concept

2. **Introduce the Stillness**
   - Start with 10-second holds, build to 42 measures
   - Focus on posture, breath control, no swaying
   - Mental preparation: "You are the Gate"

3. **Rehearse the Transformation Ritual**
   - Separate from full run-throughs (dedicated block time)
   - Drill jacket/hat removal choreography
   - Build synchronization and muscle memory

4. **Clean Baba Yaga Drill Fundamentals**
   - Teach curved path technique
   - Introduce vortex patterns
   - Emphasize musicality and flow

**Deliverables:**
- Members understand the formations and concepts
- Foundation is laid for summer refinement
- Video documentation of progress (for staff reference)

**Time Commitment:** 5-7 days, full-time (approximately 50-60 hours)

---

### Phase 3: Summer Tour Support (July-August 2026)

**On-Site Instruction (2-3 Regional Camps):**

**Focus Areas:**
1. **Clean the Stillness**
   - Video review: identify drift, posture issues
   - Micro-adjustments to spacing and alignment
   - Build endurance (full 42-measure runs)

2. **Refine the Transformation Ritual**
   - Tighten synchronization
   - Ensure placement precision (jackets/hats in straight lines)
   - Rehearse under show conditions (with music, in uniform)

3. **Polish Baba Yaga Drill**
   - Clean transitions between formations
   - Refine vortex timing and clarity
   - Emphasize musicality

4. **Support Visual Staff**
   - Assist with sectionals or individual member coaching
   - Provide feedback on execution challenges
   - Help troubleshoot any drill-related issues

**Deliverables:**
- Execution is cleaner week-over-week
- Members gain confidence in the stillness and transformation
- Show is Finals-ready by early August

**Time Commitment:** 2-3 camps × 3-4 days each = 6-12 days (approximately 60-100 hours)

---

### Phase 4: Finals Week (August 2026)

**On-Site Instruction (Finals Week):**

**Focus Areas:**
1. **Final Refinements**
   - Last-minute cleaning based on Semifinals performance
   - Mental preparation for the Finals-only transformation reveal
   - Ensure DM is confident in the final salute and exit sequence

2. **Support Staff**
   - Available for any last-minute adjustments
   - Provide encouragement and perspective
   - Be present for the moment

**Deliverables:**
- Show is executed at its absolute peak
- Members are confident and prepared
- Staff feels supported

**Time Commitment:** 4-5 days (approximately 40-50 hours)

# 4. COLLABORATION WITH ACADEMY VISUAL STAFF

---

## How We Work Together

### Model 1: Co-Design (If Academy Wants Drill Design Support)

**Process:**
1. Academy's visual staff provides overall show structure and concept
2. I collaborate on drill writing (specific formations, transitions, coordinates)
3. We review and refine together (remote collaboration via video calls)
4. I attend camps to teach what we've designed

**Advantage:** Shared creative ownership, combined expertise

---

### Model 2: Execution Specialist (If Academy Has Drill Designer Already)

**Process:**
1. Academy's visual staff writes the drill
2. I review the drill and provide feedback (execution feasibility, demand scaling)
3. I attend camps to clean and refine what's been written
4. Visual staff maintains creative control; I focus on execution

**Advantage:** Clear division of labor, visual staff leads design

---

### Model 3: Consultant (Minimal Involvement)

**Process:**
1. Academy's visual staff designs and teaches the drill independently
2. I attend 1-2 camps as a guest instructor (fresh eyes, specific feedback)
3. I provide remote video review as needed

**Advantage:** Lower cost, less commitment, Academy maintains full control

---

## Recommended Model: Model 2 (Execution Specialist)

**Why:**
- Academy likely already has visual staff on contract
- I bring specialized expertise (stillness, transformation ritual, interwoven grid)
- Clear roles: Visual staff = creative lead, I = execution partner
- This model respects Academy's existing structure while adding value

---

**Includes:**

# 7. EXPECTED OUTCOMES

## What Academy Can Expect

### By End of Spring Training Camp (June 2026):
- Members understand the square perimeter formation and interwoven grid
- Stillness foundation is established (10-20 second holds, building toward 42 measures)
- Transformation ritual is introduced and rehearsed
- Baba Yaga drill fundamentals are taught

### By Mid-Season (July 2026):
- Stillness is clean (no drift, solid posture, 42-measure endurance)
- Transformation ritual is synchronized and precise
- Baba Yaga drill is cleaned and musical
- Show is scoring in the 94-95 range (early season)

### By Finals Week (August 2026):
- Execution is at peak (stillness is flawless, transformation is seamless)
- Members are confident and committed to the bold choices
- Show is scoring in the 95-97 range
- Academy places 4th-6th (massive improvement from 16th)

### Long-Term (2027 and Beyond):
- Members carry forward the discipline and precision learned
- Academy's reputation shifts: "They're not a mid-tier corps anymore—they're contenders"
- Recruiting improves (members want to march the corps that did "The Gate")
- Staff confidence increases (they executed a top-tier show concept)

---

## Metrics of Success

### Execution Quality:
- Stillness: Zero visible drift, solid posture held for 42 measures
- Transformation: Synchronized within 1-2 seconds, jackets/hats placed cleanly
- Interwoven grid: Blend is pristine, intonation is clean

### Scoring:
- Music Effect: 19.8-20 / 20
- Visual Effect: 19.8-20 / 20
- General Effect: 19.7-20 / 20
- Total Score: 95-97 (Year 1), 96.5-97.5 (Year 2 if refined)

### Placement:
- Year 1: 4th-6th place (Top 6 breakthrough)
- Year 2: 2nd-4th place (Medal contention)

### Intangibles:
- Members feel proud and empowered
- Staff feels supported and confident
- Academy's reputation transforms

## Teaching Philosophy

**"Drill is not about hitting dots. It's about creating impact."**

My approach:
1. **Teach the WHY before the HOW**
   - Members need to understand the design intent
   - "We're standing still because stillness = power, not because we can't march"

2. **Build incrementally**
   - Start simple, add complexity gradually
   - Celebrate small victories (10-second hold → 42-measure hold)

3. **Use video ruthlessly**
   - Members see themselves, understand what needs fixing
   - Video doesn't lie—it's objective feedback

4. **Empower members**
   - "You are not executing someone else's vision. This is YOUR show. Own it."

5. **Support staff**
   - I'm here to help, not take over
   - Visual staff leads, I support

- Former students/members
- Colleagues in the marching arts community

**"The Gate" Total: $26,257 - $45,507**

- **Low estimate:** $2,343 BELOW typical low end
- **High estimate:** $15,000 BELOW typical high end

**Why "The Gate" Costs Less:**
1. **Local sourcing** (Albuquerque creative network = lower labor costs)
2. **Prototype-first approach** (test cheap, build once = less waste)
3. **Lightweight materials** (PVC, silk = affordable and durable)
4. **Existing uniform base** (white jackets, black pants already owned)
5. **Efficient design** (minimal drill changes = less rehearsal time = lower overall costs)

# 4. COST-SAVING STRATEGIES

## Strategy 1: Prototype Before Committing

**Approach:**
- Invest $2,350 - $3,900 in prototypes FIRST
- Test the Hut, Phoenix flag, and guard costumes
- Make GO/NO-GO decision after seeing proof-of-concept

**Benefit:**
- Reduces risk of full-scale production failure
- Allows design adjustments before expensive final production
- Builds confidence in feasibility

**Academy's Investment:**
- Prototypes: $2,350 - $3,900 (upfront)
- If GO: Proceed with full production ($23,907 - $41,607 additional)
- If NO-GO: Academy keeps prototypes (can repurpose or use for future shows)

---

## Strategy 2: Phased Production Schedule

**Approach:**
- Phase 1 (January-March): Prototypes + music arrangement
- Phase 2 (April-May): Props (Hut, Phoenix, podium)
- Phase 3 (May-June): Costumes (guard first, then brass/battery)

**Benefit:**
- Spreads costs over 6 months (easier on cash flow)
- Allows mid-course corrections if needed
- Reduces financial burden on any single month

---

## Strategy 3: Local Sourcing & DIY Where Possible

**Approach:**
- Use Albuquerque creative network (lower labor costs than national vendors)
- Academy staff/volunteers assist with simple tasks (painting Hut, sewing hems)
- Rent or borrow equipment where possible (e.g., center podium)

**Benefit:**
- Reduces labor costs by 20-30%
- Builds corps community (members/families involved in production)

**Estimated Savings:** $1,500 - $3,000

---

## Strategy 4: Bulk Orders & Discounts

**Approach:**
- Order all guard costumes from one vendor (bulk discount)
- Order all athletic underlayers from one vendor (bulk discount)
- Negotiate with fabric suppliers (buy silk in bulk for Phoenix flag)

**Benefit:**
- 10-15% discount on large orders (typical)

**Estimated Savings:** $800 - $1,500

---

## Strategy 5: Reuse Existing Inventory

**Check Academy's Current Inventory For:**
- Portable podium (may already own one suitable for center podium)
- White jackets, black pants, black shoes (already owned—no new uniforms needed)
- PVC piping (left over from previous shows)
- Fabric remnants (can be repurposed for Hut covering)

**Estimated Savings:** $200 - $800

---

**TOTAL POTENTIAL SAVINGS: $2,500 - $6,300**

**Revised Total Cost (With Savings): $19,957 - $39,207**

---

# 5. PAYMENT SCHEDULE OPTIONS

## Option A: Full Upfront Payment

**Structure:**
- Academy pays total estimated cost upfront (January 2026)
- All vendors/contractors paid immediately
- Production begins immediately

**Benefit:**
- Fastest timeline (no waiting for payments to clear)
- Potential early-payment discounts from vendors (5-10%)

**Drawback:**
- Requires Academy to have full budget available upfront

---

## Option B: Phased Payment Schedule (Recommended)

**Structure:**

**Payment 1 (January 2026): 30% ($7,877 - $13,652)**
- Covers: Prototypes, music arrangement deposit, drill instruction deposit

**Payment 2 (April 2026): 40% ($10,503 - $18,203)**
- Covers: Props production (Hut, Phoenix, podium), music arrangement balance

**Payment 3 (June 2026): 30% ($7,877 - $13,652)**
- Covers: Costumes, drill instruction balance, contingency

**Benefit:**
- Spreads costs over 6 months (easier cash flow management)
- Academy can fundraise between payments
- Milestone-based (pay as work is completed)

---

## Option C: Milestone-Based Payments

**Structure:**
- Payment upon completion of each milestone (prototypes done, props delivered, costumes delivered, etc.)
- Flexible timing based on actual production schedule

**Benefit:**
- Academy only pays when work is verified complete
- Reduces financial risk

**Drawback:**
- Slower timeline (vendors wait for payment before starting next phase)

---

**RECOMMENDED: Option B (Phased Payment Schedule)**

# 8. MAINTENANCE & REPAIR BUDGET

## Anticipated Wear & Tear

### The Hut
**High-Risk Areas:**
- Fabric covering (wear, tears, staining)
- PVC joints (stress cracks from repeated assembly/disassembly)
- Stilt-leg mechanism (Finals version, high-stress use)

**Repair Budget:** $200 - $400 per season

**Repair Strategy:**
- Bring spare PVC connectors on tour
- Bring fabric patch kit (velcro, needle/thread)
- Albuquerque team available for mid-season repairs if needed

---

### The Phoenix Flag
**High-Risk Areas:**
- Hem tears (from weighted edge stress)
- Fabric snags (from turf, equipment contact)
- Color fading (sun exposure)

**Repair Budget:** $150 - $300 per season

**Repair Strategy:**
- Bring sewing kit on tour
- Store flag in breathable bag (prevent mildew)
- Spot-clean as needed (hand wash, air dry)

---

### Guard Costumes
**High-Risk Areas:**
- Velcro/snap fasteners (repeated use = wear out)
- Glitter outer layer (sequins fall off, fabric stress)
- Inner tunic (sweat, staining)

**Repair Budget:** $300 - $600 per season (for 32 costumes)

**Repair Strategy:**
- Bring sewing kit and spare fasteners on tour
- Dry-clean or hand-wash costumes mid-season
- Replace damaged costumes as needed

---

**TOTAL MAINTENANCE BUDGET: $650 - $1,300 per season**

---

## End-of-Season Storage

**Props:**
- Hut: Disassemble, store in dry location (shed, garage, storage unit)
- Phoenix flag: Roll or fold, store in breathable bag, dry location
- Center podium: Store with other staging equipment

**Costumes:**
- Dry-clean or hand-wash all costumes (end of season)
- Store in garment bags (guard outer layers)
- Store folded in bins (guard inner tunics, athletic underlayers)

**Storage Cost:** Minimal (fits within Academy's existing storage space)

---

# 9. RISK ASSESSMENT & CONTINGENCIES

## Risk 1: Prototype Failure

**Scenario:** Hut mechanism doesn't work as designed, Phoenix flag doesn't unfurl cleanly, guard costume quick-change is too slow.

**Mitigation:**
- Prototype FIRST (test before committing to full production)
- Multiple rounds of testing (quarter-scale, half-scale, full-scale)
- Video documentation (identify issues early)

**Contingency:**
- Redesign and rebuild prototypes (covered in prototype budget)
- Worst case: Simplify design (e.g., Hut doesn't walk, just twitches; Phoenix flag is smaller)

**Financial Impact:** Already budgeted ($2,350 - $3,900 for prototypes)

---

## Risk 2: Vendor Delays

**Scenario:** Costume vendor or fabric supplier misses deadlines, props arrive late.

**Mitigation:**
- Start early (January 2026 = 5-6 months lead time before spring camp)
- Build buffer into timeline (target April delivery, camp is June)
- Use local vendors (Albuquerque = easy to follow up in person)

**Contingency:**
- Rush fees (pay extra for expedited production/shipping)
- Simplify or scale back elements if necessary

**Financial Impact:** $500 - $1,500 (rush fees, covered by contingency budget)

---

## Risk 3: Budget Overruns

**Scenario:** Costs exceed estimates due to material price increases, unexpected repairs, or design changes.

**Mitigation:**
- Contingency budget (10% of total = $2,387 - $4,137)
- Lock in vendor quotes early (January 2026)
- Approve all design changes with cost impact analysis

**Contingency:**
- Use contingency fund (already budgeted)
- Cut non-essential elements if necessary (e.g., skip center podium if Academy already has one)

**Financial Impact:** Covered by contingency budget

---

## Risk 4: Execution Challenges

**Scenario:** Members struggle to execute stillness cleanly, transformation ritual is messy, drill is too demanding.

**Mitigation:**
- Drill instruction partnership with Sean Campbell (hands-on support, 170-240 hours over season)
- Prototype testing (ensure props/costumes are user-friendly)
- Scale demand based on Academy's current ability (design is already execution-friendly)

**Contingency:**
- Adjust drill if needed (e.g., shorten stillness from 42 measures to 30)
- Extra rehearsal time during camps (prioritize critical moments)

**Financial Impact:** Minimal (covered by drill instruction fee)

---

## Risk 5: Competitive Environment

**Scenario:** Other corps have breakout shows, judging trends shift, Academy scores lower than predicted.

**Mitigation:**
- Design is bold and effect-driven (stands out regardless of trends)
- Execution-friendly structure (minimizes risk of errors)
- Year 1 goal is Top 6, not Top 3 (realistic and achievable)

**Contingency:**
- Refine for Year 2 (if needed, run show again in 2027 with tighter execution)
- Adjust design elements based on judging feedback

**Financial Impact:** None (this is a design risk, not a budget risk)

---

**Total Cost (Low Estimate): $26,257**  
**Total Cost (High Estimate): $45,507**

## "THE GATE" - Original Show Concept

---

**NOTICE OF COPYRIGHT AND CONFIDENTIAL DISCLOSURE**

This document serves as formal notice of intellectual property rights and establishes terms for confidential disclosure of an original drum corps show concept.

---

## 1. COPYRIGHT NOTICE

**Title of Work:** "The Gate"

**Type of Work:** Original theatrical production concept for drum and bugle corps, including:
- Complete show design and narrative structure
- Visual staging concepts and formations
- Musical selection and arrangement concepts
- Prop designs and specifications
- Costume designs and transformation concepts
- Drill instruction methodology
- All supporting documentation and materials

**Author/Creator:** Sean Campbell

**Date of Creation:** [Insert date when concept was first developed—suggest the date you first started working on this, or today's date]

**Copyright Status:** © [Year] Sean Campbell. All Rights Reserved.

**Registration:** This work is protected under U.S. Copyright Law (Title 17, U.S. Code) and international copyright treaties. Formal registration with the U.S. Copyright Office is pending/completed [choose one].

---

## 2. DECLARATION OF ORIGINAL AUTHORSHIP

I, Sean Campbell, hereby declare and affirm that:

1. I am the sole creator and author of the show concept titled "The Gate"
2. All elements of this concept, including but not limited to:
   - Narrative structure and thematic concepts
   - Visual staging and formations
   - Prop designs (the Hut, Phoenix flag, etc.)
   - Costume designs (transformation concept, layered designs)
   - Drill instruction methodology
   - All written documentation and supporting materials
   
   are original works of my own creation, developed independently without infringement upon the intellectual property of any third party.

3. To the best of my knowledge, this concept does not infringe upon any existing copyrights, trademarks, or proprietary rights of any other person or entity.

4. The musical selections (Mussorgsky/Ravel) are in the public domain, and no claim of ownership is made over the underlying musical compositions. Only the concept for their use in this specific production is claimed as original work.

---

## 3. TERMS OF DISCLOSURE

### 3.1 Confidential Information

The materials contained in this pitch package, including but not limited to:
- Cover Letter
- Executive Summary
- Full Production Design Document
- Prop & Costume Portfolio
- Drill Instruction Proposal
- Budget & Logistics Overview
- This Intellectual Property Disclosure Agreement

constitute confidential and proprietary information of Sean Campbell (hereinafter "Discloser").

### 3.2 Purpose of Disclosure

This information is being disclosed to **[RECIPIENT ORGANIZATION NAME]** (hereinafter "Recipient") solely for the purpose of evaluating a potential collaboration for production of "The Gate" during the [Year] competitive season.

### 3.3 Recipient Obligations

By reviewing, receiving, or accessing these materials, Recipient agrees to:

1. **Maintain Confidentiality:** Recipient shall not disclose, publish, or disseminate any information contained in these materials to any third party without prior written consent of Discloser.

2. **Limit Use:** Recipient shall use this information solely for the purpose of evaluating the proposed collaboration. Recipient shall not use this information for any other purpose, including but not limited to:
   - Creating derivative works based on this concept
   - Sharing with other drum corps organizations
   - Using elements of this design in other productions without explicit written permission

3. **Limit Access:** Recipient shall limit access to these materials to only those individuals within the organization who have a legitimate need to review the proposal for evaluation purposes (e.g., design staff, program director, board members).

4. **Return or Destroy Materials:** Upon request by Discloser, or if Recipient declines the proposal, Recipient shall either:
   - Return all physical and digital copies of these materials to Discloser, OR
   - Certify in writing that all copies have been destroyed

### 3.4 Exceptions

Recipient's obligations under Section 3.3 shall not apply to information that:

1. Was already known to Recipient prior to disclosure by Discloser
2. Is or becomes publicly available through no fault or action of Recipient
3. Is independently developed by Recipient without reference to Discloser's materials
4. Is rightfully received by Recipient from a third party without confidentiality obligations

---

## 4. OWNERSHIP AND RIGHTS

### 4.1 Retention of Ownership

Discloser retains all right, title, and interest in and to "The Gate" concept and all related materials. No license, right, or interest in any intellectual property is granted to Recipient except as explicitly stated in a separate written agreement.

### 4.2 No Transfer of Rights by Disclosure

The disclosure of these materials does not constitute:
- A transfer of copyright or any other intellectual property rights
- A license to use, reproduce, or create derivative works
- A waiver of any rights or remedies available to Discloser
- An offer or agreement to collaborate (such agreement must be explicit and in writing)

### 4.3 Rights Upon Agreement

If Recipient and Discloser enter into a written agreement for production of "The Gate," the terms of that agreement shall govern:
- License or transfer of rights (if any)
- Compensation and payment terms
- Credit and attribution
- Use of the concept and materials
- Any other relevant terms

Until such written agreement is executed, all rights remain exclusively with Discloser.

---

## 5. PERMITTED PITCH TO MULTIPLE ORGANIZATIONS

### 5.1 Non-Exclusive Disclosure

Discloser expressly reserves the right to pitch "The Gate" concept to multiple drum corps organizations simultaneously or sequentially. This disclosure to Recipient is **non-exclusive** unless and until a written agreement specifying exclusivity is executed.

### 5.2 Notice of Competing Pitches

Discloser has disclosed or may disclose this concept to the following organizations:
- Blue Knights Drum and Bugle Corps (Denver, CO)
- The Academy Drum and Bugle Corps (Tempe, AZ)
- [Other organizations, if applicable]

### 5.3 First-to-Commit Basis

If multiple organizations express interest in producing "The Gate," Discloser reserves the right to negotiate and contract with any interested organization. Priority may be given to the first organization to commit in writing, or at Discloser's sole discretion based on:
- Organizational fit and capability
- Proposed compensation and terms
- Production timeline
- Other relevant factors

### 5.4 Notice of Agreement

If Discloser enters into an agreement with another organization for production of "The Gate," Discloser shall provide written notice to Recipient. Upon such notice, Recipient's right to negotiate for this concept terminates, and Recipient's confidentiality obligations under Section 3.3 continue in perpetuity.

---

## 6. CREDIT AND ATTRIBUTION

### 6.1 Required Credit

If Recipient produces "The Gate" pursuant to a written agreement with Discloser, Recipient agrees to provide appropriate credit and attribution to Sean Campbell in all materials related to the production, including but not limited to:
- Program books
- Announcements
- Marketing materials
- Social media
- Press releases

### 6.2 Form of Credit

Credit shall be in substantially the following form, unless otherwise agreed in writing:

> **"THE GATE"**  
> Original Concept, Design, and Drill

- Adjust the budget
- Change design elements
- Modify my involvement
- Alter the timeline
- Or discuss anything else

**Let's talk.** I'm flexible and interested in finding a partnership that works for both of us.
